   le travail reste un angle mort des travaux sociologiques consacrÃ©s aux
   mÃ©tiers de la santÃ©. Au-delÃ  des reprÃ©sentations sociales dominantes de
   lâ€™ambulancier Â« transporteur Â», lâ€™enquÃªte rÃ©vÃ¨le les multiples tÃ¢ches
   de soins quâ€™il rÃ©alise et notamment, les soins techniques pratiquÃ©s

   This article represents a contribution to the sociology of work and to
   the sociology of occupations. The author undertook a direct
   participatory observation of the day-to-day lives of French private
   ambulance drivers, whose work remains a blind spot in sociological
   research dedicated to the healthcare professions. Beyond the dominant
   social representation of the ambulance driver as a â€œtransporterâ€, the
   enquiry reveals the multiple care tasks that they undertake, in
   particular the technical care practised within the framework of
   emergency health transport. In 2007, the creation of the state degree
   for ambulance drivers, which sought to extend their healthcare remit in
   this domain, signalled a turning point in the history of this
   professional group. It provided an opportunity to satisfy the claims of
   a section of the group that was seeking to acquire the status of
   emergency specialists by drawing on the example of European and
   American ambulance paramedics. However, despite favourable
   technological and scientific factors, the outcome of this process of
   segmentation still remains uncertain today, partly because of obstacles
   internal to the professional group, but also because of the political
   and corporatist barriers in its way.

   Sylvie Morel

   Citation | Auteur

RÃ©sumÃ©s

   FranÃ§ais English

   Cet article propose une contribution Ã  la sociologie du travail et Ã  la
   sociologie des professions. Lâ€™auteure sâ€™est livrÃ©e Ã  une observation
   participante directe du quotidien des ambulanciers privÃ©s franÃ§ais dont
   le travail reste un angle mort des travaux sociologiques consacrÃ©s aux
   mÃ©tiers de la santÃ©. Au-delÃ  des reprÃ©sentations sociales dominantes de
   lâ€™ambulancier Â« transporteur Â», lâ€™enquÃªte rÃ©vÃ¨le les multiples tÃ¢ches
   de soins quâ€™il rÃ©alise et notamment, les soins techniques pratiquÃ©s
   dans le cadre de transports sanitaires dâ€™urgence. En 2007, la crÃ©ation
   du diplÃ´me dâ€™Ã‰tat dâ€™ambulancier, qui prÃ©voit un Ã©largissement de leur
   mandat sanitaire dans ce domaine, marque un tournant dans lâ€™histoire de
   ce groupe professionnel. Il constitue une opportunitÃ© de satisfaire les
   revendications dâ€™un segment du groupe qui cherche Ã  conquÃ©rir le statut
   de spÃ©cialiste de lâ€™urgence en sâ€™appuyant sur lâ€™exemple des
   ambulanciers paramedics europÃ©ens et amÃ©ricains. Toutefois, en dÃ©pit de

   This article represents a contribution to the sociology of work and to
   the sociology of occupations. The author undertook a direct
   participatory observation of the day-to-day lives of French private
   ambulance drivers, whose work remains a blind spot in sociological
   research dedicated to the healthcare professions. Beyond the dominant
   social representation of the ambulance driver as a â€œtransporterâ€, the
   enquiry reveals the multiple care tasks that they undertake, in
   particular the technical care practised within the framework of
   emergency health transport. In 2007, the creation of the state degree
   for ambulance drivers, which sought to extend their healthcare remit in
   this domain, signalled a turning point in the history of this
   professional group. It provided an opportunity to satisfy the claims of
   a section of the group that was seeking to acquire the status of
   emergency specialists by drawing on the example of European and
   American ambulance paramedics. However, despite favourable
   technological and scientific factors, the outcome of this process of
   segmentation still remains uncertain today, partly because of obstacles
   internal to the professional group, but also because of the political
   and corporatist barriers in its way.

Les politiques du genre face au conflit

   Guerre de la drogue et politiques de genre au Mexique
   Wartime Gender Politics in Mexico. War Against Drug Trafficking and the
   Politics of Gender in Mexico
   Mathieu Caulier
   p. 303-324
   RÃ©sumÃ© | Index | Plan | Texte | Bibliographie | Notes | Citation |
   Auteur

RÃ©sumÃ©s

   FranÃ§ais English

   Le genre comme concept dâ€™entendement des problÃ©matiques sociales et
   comme catÃ©gorie dâ€™action pour les politiques publiques a connu un
   dÃ©veloppement remarquable dans les annÃ©es 1990. BÃ©nÃ©ficiant de
   militantes et dâ€™expertes engagÃ©es dans la modification des politiques
   publiques, le contexte mexicain fut propice Ã  la crÃ©ation
   dâ€™institutions et de programmes sociaux adoptant une Â« perspective de
   genre Â». Cependant, la violence armÃ©e et sa rÃ©ponse Ã©tatique ont
   progressivement conquis les espaces politique et mÃ©diatique mexicains
   et relÃ©guÃ© les politiques avec perspective de genre loin dans lâ€™ordre
   des prioritÃ©s de lâ€™action publique. Cet article analyse les Ã©lÃ©ments de
   la problÃ©matique en faisant porter la focale sur le peu dâ€™attention
   politique portÃ©e au(x) fÃ©minicide(s), sur les restrictions budgÃ©taires

   militantes Ã  influer sur les politiques actuelles depuis lâ€™arrivÃ©e au

   Parti de la RÃ©volution Institutionnelle (pri) Ã  la tÃªte de lâ€™Ã‰tat en
   2012.

   Gender as a concept of understanding of social issues and as a category
   of action for public policy has undergone a remarkable development in
   the 1990s in Mexico. Relying on activists and experts involved in
   changing public policies, the Mexican context was conducive to the
   creation of institutions and social programs adopting a Â« gender
   perspective Â». However, armed violence and state response gradually
   conquered the Mexican political and media spaces. This contributed to
   the relegation of policies with a gender perspective far away in the
   order of priorities of public action. This article analyzes the

   public policy since the coming to power of the Partido AcciÃ³n Nacional
   (pan) in 2000, and the return of the Party of the Institutional
   Revolution (pri) at the head of the state in 2012.
